Tammy Baldwin: The American Relief Act, 2025. As I consider this bill, I'm reminded of the importance of providing relief to those affected by natural disasters and supporting our nation's farmers. The allocation of $100 billion for disaster relief efforts, including $29 billion for FEMA and $21 billion for agricultural assistance, is a crucial step in helping communities recover from the devastating effects of hurricanes Helene and Milton.

I also appreciate the extension of the 2018 Farm Bill through September 30, 2025, which will provide continued access to critical programs like crop insurance, Price Loss Coverage, and Agriculture Risk Coverage. This will bring much-needed stability to our agricultural sector, particularly in Wisconsin, where farming is a vital part of our economy.

Furthermore, the additional $10 billion in economic assistance to crop producers facing economic losses due to declining crop prices and elevated production costs is a welcome provision. Our farmers have been facing significant challenges in recent years, and this support will help them stay afloat during these difficult times.

As a Democrat, I'm pleased to see that this bill has received bipartisan support in the House, with 366 votes in favor and only 34 against. While I may have some reservations about certain aspects of the bill, I believe that the overall package is a positive step forward.

Therefore, I will be voting in favor of the American Relief Act, 2025. I urge my colleagues to join me in supporting this important legislation, which will provide critical relief to those in need and help our nation's farmers and communities thrive.

Let us put aside our differences and come together to pass the American Relief Act, 2025.

Rand Paul: The American Relief Act, 2025.  I've given this bill a lot of thought, and I have to say, I'm disappointed.  As a senator who's always been committed to fiscal responsibility, I just can't bring myself to support a bill that adds $100 billion to our national debt without any offsets.

Now, I understand that disaster relief and agricultural assistance are important, and I'm not opposed to providing help to those in need.  But we have to be responsible about how we do it.  We can't just keep borrowing money from China to fund our spending habits.  It's unsustainable, and it's going to hurt our economy in the long run.

I've heard my colleagues talk about the importance of providing relief to those affected by natural disasters, and I agree with that.  But we have to do it in a way that's fiscally responsible.  We can't just throw money at the problem without thinking about the consequences.

I'm also concerned about the extension of the 2018 Farm Bill.  While I support the programs that are included in the bill, I think we need to take a closer look at how they're working and make sure that we're not wasting taxpayer dollars.

So, I'm afraid I'll be voting no on the American Relief Act, 2025.  I know it's not a popular decision, but I think it's the right one.  We need to be more responsible with our spending, and we need to start thinking about the long-term consequences of our actions.

To my colleagues who are supporting this bill, I would say that I understand your desire to help those in need, but we have to do it in a way that's responsible and sustainable.  Let's work together to find a better solution, one that doesn't add to our national debt and doesn't hurt our economy in the long run.

And to Senators Murray, Ossoff, and Padilla, I would say that I appreciate your comments, but I have to respectfully disagree.  While I understand the importance of providing relief to those affected by natural disasters, I think we need to be more careful about how we do it.  We can't just keep spending money without thinking about the consequences.  Let's work together to find a better solution, one that's fiscally responsible and sustainable.

As a senator who has consistently advocated for the needs of rural communities and our nation's farmers, I am pleased to see the inclusion of $10 billion in economic assistance to crop producers facing economic losses due to declining crop prices and elevated production costs. This provision will provide much-needed support to Tennessee's farmers and rural communities, who have been hit hard by recent natural disasters. I also appreciate the allocation of $12 billion in grants through the Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) to assist affected communities, which will provide much-needed support to our state's economy.

However, I do have concerns about the bill's impact on our national debt and the potential long-term costs. As a nation, we must be mindful of our fiscal responsibilities and ensure that we are not mortgaging our future for short-term gains. Nevertheless, I believe that the urgent need for disaster relief and agricultural assistance outweighs the potential long-term costs.

I would like to commend my colleagues, Senators Young, Baldwin, Barrasso, and Bennet, for their thoughtful comments on the bill. I share their commitment to providing relief to those affected by natural disasters and supporting our nation's farmers. I also appreciate the comments from Senator Rick Scott, who highlighted the importance of disaster relief and agricultural assistance for his home state of Florida.

In particular, I would like to highlight the importance of the Farm Bill extension, which will allow continued access to critical programs like crop insurance, Price Loss Coverage (PLC), and Agriculture Risk Coverage (ARC). This will provide much-needed support to farmers and rural communities, who rely on these programs to make ends meet.

As a representative of Tennessee, I am also pleased to see the support for our nation's agricultural industry in this bill. The agricultural industry is a vital part of our state's economy, and I am committed to doing everything I can to support our farmers.

In conclusion, I urge my colleagues to join me in supporting the American Relief Act, 2025. This bill is a crucial step in providing relief to those affected by natural disasters and supporting our nation's farmers. Let us come together to support this important legislation and show the American people that we can work together to support those in need. I will be voting yes on this bill.

I must say, I am heartened to see the bipartisan support for this bill, with 366 votes in favor and only 34 against in the House. This level of support demonstrates that we can put aside our differences and come together to support those in need. I hope that this spirit of bipartisanship will continue as we move forward with this legislation.

As a senator from Oregon, I have seen firsthand the devastating impact of natural disasters on our communities, particularly in the aftermath of recent wildfires and droughts that have affected our state.

I am pleased to see the allocation of $100 billion for disaster relief efforts, including $29 billion for FEMA and $21 billion for agricultural assistance. This investment will help communities recover from the devastating effects of recent natural disasters. The inclusion of $10 billion in economic assistance to crop producers facing economic losses due to declining crop prices and elevated production costs is also a crucial provision that will provide much-needed support to Oregon's farmers and rural communities.

The Farm Bill extension, which will allow continued access to critical programs like crop insurance, Price Loss Coverage (PLC), and Agriculture Risk Coverage (ARC), is also a vital component of this legislation. Our farmers and rural communities rely on these programs to stay afloat, and I'm committed to ensuring they have the support they need.

While I understand the concerns about the bill's impact on our national debt, I believe that the urgent need for disaster relief and agricultural assistance outweighs the potential long-term costs. As a nation, we have a moral obligation to support those affected by natural disasters and to provide relief to our farmers and rural communities.

I appreciate the thoughtful comments from my colleagues, Senators Lummis, Markey, Marshall, and McConnell, and I am heartened to see the bipartisan support for this bill, with 366 votes in favor and only 34 against in the House. This level of support demonstrates that we can put aside our differences and come together to support those in need.

In conclusion, I urge my colleagues to join me in supporting the American Relief Act, 2025. This bill is a crucial step in providing relief to those affected by natural disasters and supporting our nation's farmers. Let us come together to support this important legislation and show the American people that we can work together to support those in need. I will be voting yes on this bill.

I understand and share their concerns, but I believe that we must prioritize the urgent needs of those affected by natural disasters and our nation's farmers. I am willing to work with my colleagues to find ways to improve the bill and address their concerns, but I will not let objections stand in the way of providing critical relief to those who need it most.

While I agree that disaster relief and agricultural assistance are essential, I believe that we must prioritize these efforts within the context of our nation's fiscal constraints. The allocation of $100 billion for disaster relief efforts, including $29 billion for FEMA and $21 billion for agricultural assistance, is a significant investment, but we must consider the long-term implications of such spending on our national debt.

I'm also concerned about the lack of offsets in this bill. We're essentially borrowing money to fund these relief efforts, which will only add to our nation's already staggering debt. As a nation, we have a moral obligation to support those affected by natural disasters, but we also have a responsibility to be prudent stewards of taxpayer dollars.

I'd like to ask my colleagues, have we considered alternative solutions that could provide relief to those in need without resorting to additional borrowing? Have we explored ways to streamline our disaster relief efforts, to make them more efficient and effective, without breaking the bank?

I'm not opposed to providing relief to those affected by natural disasters, but I believe we must do so in a fiscally responsible manner. I urge my colleagues to consider the long-term consequences of our actions and to work with me to find more sustainable solutions.

As for the Farm Bill extension, I support the provision of critical programs like crop insurance, Price Loss Coverage (PLC), and Agriculture Risk Coverage (ARC), but I believe we must also consider the impact of these programs on our nation's agricultural sector as a whole.

In conclusion, while I understand the urgency of the situation and the need for relief, I will be voting no on the American Relief Act, 2025. I believe that we can do better, that we can find more fiscally responsible solutions that balance our nation's compassion with our nation's fiscal realities. I urge my colleagues to join me in seeking alternative solutions that prioritize both relief and responsibility.

-------This is the conversation summary--------
The American Relief Act, 2025, is a comprehensive bill that addresses the urgent needs of those affected by recent natural disasters and provides substantial support to our nation's farmers. The bill allocates $100 billion for disaster relief efforts, including $29 billion for FEMA and $21 billion for agricultural assistance. The inclusion of $10 billion in economic assistance to crop producers facing economic losses due to declining crop prices and elevated production costs is also a crucial provision that will provide much-needed support to our nation's farmers and rural communities.

The Farm Bill extension, which will allow continued access to critical programs like crop insurance, Price Loss Coverage (PLC), and Agriculture Risk Coverage (ARC), is also a vital component of this legislation. Our farmers and rural communities rely on these programs to stay afloat, and I'm committed to ensuring they have the support they need.

While I understand the concerns about the bill's impact on our national debt, I believe that the urgent need for disaster relief and agricultural assistance outweighs the potential long-term costs. As a nation, we have a moral obligation to support those affected by natural disasters and to provide relief to our farmers and rural communities.
